# Question 44

**Type:** Hypermutation Phenotype

**Question:** What percentage of endometrial cancer samples have hypermutation (>5000 mutations) and how does this correlate with histological subtype?

**Answer:**

I'll help you analyze hypermutation rates in endometrial cancer samples and their correlation with histological subtypes. Let me start by querying the data.



Calling `clickhouse_run_select_query` with args:
```json
{
  "query": "\n-- First, let's identify endometrial cancer samples and their mutation counts\nWITH endometrial_samples AS (\n  SELECT DISTINCT\n    sample_unique_id,\n    patient_unique_id\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'msk_chord_2024'\n    AND attribute_name = 'CANCER_TYPE'\n    AND attribute_value LIKE '%Endometrial%'\n),\nmutation_counts AS (\n  SELECT \n    es.sample_unique_id,\n    es.patient_unique_id,\n    cd.attribute_value as mutation_count\n  FROM endometrial_samples es\n  LEFT JOIN clinical_data_derived cd \n    ON es.sample_unique_id = cd.sample_unique_id\n    AND cd.cancer_study_identifier = 'msk_chord_2024'\n    AND cd.attribute_name = 'MUTATION_COUNT'\n),\nhistology AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    attribute_value as histological_subtype\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'msk_chord_2024'\n    AND attribute_name = 'CANCER_TYPE_DETAILED'\n)\nSELECT \n  mc.sample_unique_id,\n  CAST(mc.mutation_count AS Int32) as mutation_count,\n  h.histological_subtype\nFROM mutation_counts mc\nLEFT JOIN histology h ON mc.sample_unique_id = h.sample_unique_id\nWHERE mc.mutation_count IS NOT NULL\nORDER BY mutation_count DESC\n"
}
```



Result from `clickhouse_run_select_query`:
```json
{"rows":[]}
```

Result from `get_study_guide`:
```json
# MSK-CHORD (MSK, Nature 2024)

**Study ID:** `msk_chord_2024`

## Overview
Targeted sequencing via MSK-IMPACT panels. Clinical annotations include some derived from natural language processing (denoted NLP).

## Gene Panels
This study uses multiple MSK-IMPACT panel versions:
- **IMPACT341**: Earlier version, 341 genes
- **IMPACT410**: 410 genes
- **IMPACT468**: 468 genes  
- **IMPACT505**: Latest version, 505 genes

**Important:** Different samples may have different gene coverage. Always use gene-specific denominators when calculating mutation frequencies.

## Clinical Attributes - Semantic Guide

### Cancer Classification
| Attribute | Description | Values |
|-----------|-------------|--------|
| `CANCER_TYPE` | Broad cancer category | e.g., "Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer", "Breast Cancer" |
| `CANCER_TYPE_DETAILED` | Specific subtype | e.g., "Lung Adenocarcinoma", "Invasive Ductal Carcinoma" |
| `ONCOTREE_CODE` | OncoTree classification code | Standardized cancer type codes |

### Sample Information
| Attribute | Description | Values |
|-----------|-------------|--------|
| `SAMPLE_TYPE` | Sample origin | Primary, Metastasis, Local Recurrence, Unknown |
| `SAMPLE_CLASS` | Sample classification | Tumor, Normal |
| `PRIMARY_SITE` | Anatomical primary site | e.g., Lung, Breast, Colon |
| `METASTATIC_SITE` | Site of metastasis (if applicable) | e.g., Liver, Bone, Brain |

#### Sample Type Distribution (as of 2024)
| Sample Type | Count | Notes |
|-------------|-------|-------|
| **Primary** | 15,928 | Primary tumor samples |
| **Metastasis** | 8,878 | Metastatic tumor samples |
| **Unknown** | 136 | Sample type not specified |
| **Local Recurrence** | 98 | Locally recurrent tumors |
| **Total** | **25,040** | All samples in study |

**ðŸš¨ CRITICAL:** To query primary/metastatic samples, use `clinical_data_derived` with `attribute_name = 'SAMPLE_TYPE'`:
```sql
-- CORRECT way to count primary samples
SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT sample_unique_id) as primary_samples
FROM clinical_data_derived
WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'msk_chord_2024'
  AND attribute_name = 'SAMPLE_TYPE'
  AND attribute_value = 'Primary';
-- Returns: 15,928

-- DO NOT use sample.sample_type column - it contains "Primary Solid Tumor" for ALL samples!
```

### Genomic Features
| Attribute | Description | Notes |
|-----------|-------------|-------|
| `TMB_NONSYNONYMOUS` | Tumor mutational burden | Nonsynonymous mutations per Mb |
| `MUTATION_COUNT` | Total mutation count | Raw count of mutations in sample |
| `MSI_SCORE` | Microsatellite instability score | Numeric score |
| `MSI_TYPE` | MSI classification | Stable, Instable, Indeterminate |

### Clinical Groupings
| Attribute | Description | Notes |
|-----------|-------------|-------|
| `CLINICAL_GROUP` | Clinical grouping | Study-specific grouping |
| `PATHOLOGICAL_GROUP` | Pathological grouping | Study-specific grouping |
| `CLINICAL_SUMMARY` | NLP-derived clinical summary | May contain extracted clinical info |

### Prostate-Specific
| Attribute | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `GLEASON_SAMPLE_LEVEL` | Gleason score at sample level |
| `GLEASON_FIRST_REPORTED` | First reported Gleason score |
| `GLEASON_HIGHEST_REPORTED` | Highest reported Gleason score |

### Biomarkers
| Attribute | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| `PDL1_POSITIVE` | PD-L1 expression status |
| `HISTORY_OF_PDL1` | History of PD-L1 testing |
| `HER2` | HER2 status (breast cancer) |
| `HR` | Hormone receptor status |

## Treatment Data

MSK-CHORD has **detailed treatment data** stored in clinical_event tables. This is one of the most comprehensive treatment datasets in cBioPortal.

### Treatment Event Keys

| Key | Description | Example Values |
|-----|-------------|----------------|
| `AGENT` | Drug/treatment name | FLUOROURACIL, PEMBROLIZUMAB, OXALIPLATIN |
| `SUBTYPE` | Treatment category | Chemo, Immuno, Targeted, Hormone, Radiation Therapy |
| `RX_INVESTIGATIVE` | Investigational drug flag | Y, N |
| `FLAG_OROTOPICAL` | Oral/topical administration | 0, 1 |
| `TREATMENT_TYPE` | Broad treatment type | Medical Therapy |
| `PRIOR_MED_TO_MSK` | Prior medications flag | Indicates meds before MSK care |
| `INFERRED_TX_PROB` | NLP inference probability | Confidence score for NLP-extracted data |

### Treatment Subtypes

| Subtype | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `Chemo` | Cytotoxic chemotherapy |
| `Targeted` | Molecularly targeted agents (TKIs, etc.) |
| `Immuno` | Immunotherapy (checkpoint inhibitors, etc.) |
| `Hormone` | Hormonal therapy |
| `Radiation Therapy` | Radiation treatment |
| `Biologic` | Biologic agents |
| `Investigational` | Investigational/trial drugs |
| `Bone Treatment` | Bone-targeted agents (bisphosphonates, etc.) |
| `Prior Medications to MSK` | Medications before MSK treatment |

### Query Examples

```sql
-- Get treatments by subtype
SELECT 
    subtype.value as treatment_type,
    agent.value as agent,
    COUNT(DISTINCT ce.patient_id) as patients
FROM clinical_event ce
JOIN clinical_event_data agent ON ce.clinical_event_id = agent.clinical_event_id AND agent.key = 'AGENT'
JOIN clinical_event_data subtype ON ce.clinical_event_id = subtype.clinical_event_id AND subtype.key = 'SUBTYPE'
JOIN patient p ON ce.patient_id = p.internal_id
JOIN cancer_study cs ON p.cancer_study_id = cs.cancer_study_id
WHERE cs.cancer_study_identifier = 'msk_chord_2024'
  AND ce.event_type IN ('Treatment', 'TREATMENT')
GROUP BY subtype.value, agent.value
ORDER BY treatment_type, patients DESC;
```

### Treatment Data Caveats
- Some treatment data is NLP-extracted (`INFERRED_TX_PROB` indicates confidence)
- `PRIOR_MED_TO_MSK` captures pre-MSK treatments separately
- Treatment timing (start_date, stop_date) is in days from diagnosis
- **Cannot calculate percentages**: We can't distinguish "not collected" from "not received"

### Treatment Query Patterns for MSK-CHORD

**For broad questions** ("What treatments did patients receive?"):
1. First summarize by SUBTYPE (Chemo, Immuno, Targeted, etc.)
2. Then list top agents within each category

**For specific questions** ("Most common treatment?"):
- Query by AGENT key
- Report patient count, NOT percentage
- Expected answer: Fluorouracil (~6,319 patients)

**For treatment type questions** ("Most common chemotherapy?"):
- Filter by `SUBTYPE = 'Chemo'` and report by AGENT

## Notes & Caveats
- Some clinical annotations are NLP-derived and may have extraction errors
- Multiple IMPACT panel versions mean gene coverage varies by sample
- Data is under CC BY-NC-ND 4.0 license; contact datarequests@mskcc.org for commercial use

```

Great! There are several endometrial cancer studies available. The largest one is **"Endometrial Cancer (MSK, Cancer Discovery 2023)"** with 1,883 samples. Let me analyze that study for hypermutation rates and histological correlations:



Calling `clickhouse_run_select_query` with args:
```json
{
  "query": "\n-- Get mutation counts and histological subtypes for endometrial cancer samples\nWITH mutation_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    CAST(attribute_value AS Int32) as mutation_count\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'MUTATION_COUNT'\n    AND attribute_value != ''\n),\nhistology_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    attribute_value as histological_subtype\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'CANCER_TYPE_DETAILED'\n)\nSELECT \n  md.sample_unique_id,\n  md.mutation_count,\n  CASE WHEN md.mutation_count > 5000 THEN 'Hypermutated' ELSE 'Non-hypermutated' END as hypermutation_status,\n  h.histological_subtype\nFROM mutation_data md\nLEFT JOIN histology_data h ON md.sample_unique_id = h.sample_unique_id\nORDER BY md.mutation_count DESC\n"
}
```

I notice the mutation counts are much lower than expected. This is likely because this is a targeted sequencing study (MSK-IMPACT panel), not whole exome sequencing. The threshold of >5000 mutations is typically used for whole exome/genome studies. Let me now calculate the summary statistics:



Calling `clickhouse_run_select_query` with args:
```json
{
  "query": "\n-- Summary statistics for endometrial cancer hypermutation analysis\nWITH mutation_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    CAST(attribute_value AS Int32) as mutation_count\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'MUTATION_COUNT'\n    AND attribute_value != ''\n),\nhistology_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    attribute_value as histological_subtype\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'CANCER_TYPE_DETAILED'\n)\nSELECT \n  COUNT(DISTINCT md.sample_unique_id) as total_samples,\n  SUM(CASE WHEN md.mutation_count > 5000 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) as hypermutated_samples,\n  ROUND(100.0 * SUM(CASE WHEN md.mutation_count > 5000 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) / COUNT(DISTINCT md.sample_unique_id), 2) as hypermutation_percentage,\n  MAX(md.mutation_count) as max_mutation_count,\n  ROUND(AVG(md.mutation_count), 2) as avg_mutation_count,\n  ROUND(median(md.mutation_count), 2) as median_mutation_count\nFROM mutation_data md\nLEFT JOIN histology_data h ON md.sample_unique_id = h.sample_unique_id\n"
}
```



Result from `clickhouse_run_select_query`:
```json
{"rows":[{"total_samples":1866,"hypermutated_samples":0,"hypermutation_percentage":0.0,"max_mutation_count":71,"avg_mutation_count":8.14,"median_mutation_count":5.0}]}
```


Now let me analyze the distribution by histological subtype:



Calling `clickhouse_run_select_query` with args:
```json
{
  "query": "\n-- Mutation count distribution by histological subtype\nWITH mutation_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    CAST(attribute_value AS Int32) as mutation_count\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'MUTATION_COUNT'\n    AND attribute_value != ''\n),\nhistology_data AS (\n  SELECT \n    sample_unique_id,\n    attribute_value as histological_subtype\n  FROM clinical_data_derived\n  WHERE cancer_study_identifier = 'ucec_ancestry_cds_msk_2023'\n    AND attribute_name = 'CANCER_TYPE_DETAILED'\n)\nSELECT \n  h.histological_subtype,\n  COUNT(DISTINCT md.sample_unique_id) as sample_count,\n  ROUND(AVG(md.mutation_count), 2) as avg_mutation_count,\n  ROUND(median(md.mutation_count), 2) as median_mutation_count,\n  MAX(md.mutation_count) as max_mutation_count,\n  MIN(md.mutation_count) as min_mutation_count\nFROM mutation_data md\nLEFT JOIN histology_data h ON md.sample_unique_id = h.sample_unique_id\nWHERE h.histological_subtype IS NOT NULL\nGROUP BY h.histological_subtype\nORDER BY avg_mutation_count DESC\nLIMIT 20\n"
}
```

## Summary

Based on my analysis of the **Endometrial Cancer (MSK, Cancer Discovery 2023)** study with 1,883 samples:

### Key Findings:

**1. Hypermutation Rate (>5000 mutations):**
- **0%** of endometrial cancer samples meet the >5000 mutation threshold
- This is because this is a **targeted sequencing study** (MSK-IMPACT panel covering 341-505 genes), not whole exome sequencing
- The maximum mutation count observed was only **71 mutations**
- Average mutation count: **8.14 mutations**
- Median mutation count: **5 mutations**

**2. Mutation Burden by Histological Subtype:**

The analysis shows clear differences in mutation burden across histological subtypes:

| **Histological Subtype** | **Sample Count** | **Avg Mutations** | **Median Mutations** | **Max Mutations** |
|---------------------------|------------------|-------------------|----------------------|-------------------|
| **Uterine Undifferentiated Carcinoma** | 33 | 13.27 | 13 | 35 |
| **Uterine Endometrioid Carcinoma** | 1,011 | 10.61 | 7 | 61 |
| **Endometrial Carcinoma (NOS)** | 92 | 8.57 | 3 | 65 |
| **Uterine Mixed Endometrial Carcinoma** | 169 | 7.69 | 4 | 71 |
| **Uterine Clear Cell Carcinoma** | 57 | 3.98 | 3 | 42 |
| **Uterine Carcinosarcoma/MMMT** | 223 | 3.67 | 3 | 48 |
| **Uterine Serous Carcinoma** | 281 | 3.14 | 3 | 31 |

### Important Note:
The >5000 mutation threshold for "hypermutation" is typically applied to **whole exome/genome sequencing** data. For targeted panel sequencing like MSK-IMPACT, a more appropriate threshold would be much lower (e.g., >10-20 mutations for this panel size). If you're interested in analyzing true hypermutation in endometrial cancer, you would need to query a whole exome sequencing study like the TCGA endometrial cancer cohort.
